<Rating>4< /Rating>< Text>
By outside appearance, you might write this place off as some shady hole in the wall, or not even notice it, but that is very deceiving.  The inside is very clean with a masculine, modern style to it and just a tiny hint of 20s vintage.

The location is a reflection of the staff as well.  At first glance you might be temped to write them off as one thing or another, but regardless of what you may take from appearance, they are true professional barbers.  They won't fawn over you, but they are very friendly, welcoming, and able to give you whatever kind of cut you're looking for(and help you find out what that is in my case), all at a good price and a timely manner.

If you're looking for something other than the hospital waiting rooms of more commercial barbers, at a quality and price that beats them. I highly recommend you stop by.</Text>

<Text>While  visit  liberty station San Diego if you‚Äôre interested in US Navy history this is a great stop. There  is plenty of parking close to the ship. The ship was commissioned on July 27, 1949. It was commissioned for 18 years for much of that time it was the only landlocked ship to hold that status in the US Navy. It was used to train recruits. She is an impressive sight on land for sure! She was built to scale 2/3 the size of a Dealey class destroyer escort. She sits at the former Navy Training Center, San Diego. This ship assisted the training of over 50,000 new recruits per year, the ship still stands showing honor, courage and commitment. She is currently unused With the hopes that she will someday become a Maritime Museum. This was a must see for us.</Text>< Rating>
5<//Rating>

< review>
This "ship" was a part of the base where I attended boot camp back in 1990. We learned a great deal about ship operations & safety procedures. The worst part was going through the "Gas Chamber" room inside the "ship", You would go in and don your mask. Room fills with tear gas. You took off your mask, inhaled the gas, and then had to don your mask again. Your eyes watered and snot ran down your nose. Good times!</review>

<resp>None< /resp><username>AussieSheltieLife !</username><review>Ok - so, I want to stay here! This place is a blast for your beloved furry family member(s). Upon entering the facility, it is very cleverly designed, like a "camp". It is bright, organized and very clean! The office staff is professional, super friendly, and they will take you on a tour of the entire facility.
Your pampered pooch gets a "cabin" to themselves. For multiple pets, they get to stay  together at night, mealtimes, and there are 2 nap times, during the course of the day. In the "cabins", each camper has their own raised cot - of sturdy design, made with canvas and PVC piping. You can bring your own pups bedding if you want.
During the day, smaller dogs are put together in a large enclosure. Larger dogs are together, in other large enclosures. They can roam freely, inside and outside to play.
When the dogs are in their playtime enclosures, the employees are constantly washing and cleaning campers cabins.  It was really nice to see, such detailed maintenance and cleaning.
While you are away, log onto their website, or download their app, to watch your pup on live webcams - it's really fun to watch them play, run, and interact.
You can also drop them off for day camping too. Location is perfect, at Vasco /580, on Preston Avenue.<//review>< user_id>

Now, that's not the end of the world but they should have informed me ahead of time. Since I was leaving in two weeks, I was going to have a difficult time getting the shot taken care of before her intake day.

But I was lucky enough to be able to get a shot that day. I called CampBowWow and they told me that Shar would have to have the shot in her system for 7 days (again not explained to me when I went into the camp earlier). Again, this was still lucky because I had two weeks. They told me I needed it in her system before the interview process. Ok that's fine. I called to confirm everything. They said they could only tell me at the end of the day after the interview. I pushed and pushed and finally they said that those dates were unavailable!

Waste of time! Very unprofessional. All they needed to do was inform me of the times.

The camp itself seems nice. But the staff and the organization is extremely unprofessional and they don't care if they waste your time.<//text>

Sonny Boy would prefer to play at full speed around the clock, so Camp Bow Wow Tri-Valley helps us tremendously. A couple of full day play sessions a week with his "friends" most importantly gives him a safe and monitored opportunity to burn his crazy energy, but also gives us hours to take late classes/work late/go out to dinner without worrying about him and, considering his age and energy level, any possible destruction that comes from him being hyper and at home alone.  He typically comes home, makes a lap around the house, and heads for his bed. He absolutely loves it, and we love that he has played so hard that day that he is happily ready to rest when we get him home. The staff there is really great, and understand that Sonny is a handful. When we pick him up and ask the front desk person (usually Brandy or Francesca) how his day went, they unfailingly know with whom he had been playing, if he needed any "timeouts" to cool his jets, etc.

Sign up for a tour and their new camper interview. You won't be sorry.< /text>
